Process the current possibility and\n26047: \t     continue with the rest at next iteration.  */\n26048: \t  if (TREE_CODE (match_expr) == TRUTH_ORIF_EXPR)\n26049: \t    {\n26050: \t      next_round_match_expr = TREE_OPERAND (match_expr, 0);\n26051: \t      match_expr = TREE_OPERAND (match_expr, 1);\n26052: \t    }\n26053: \t  else\n26054: \t    next_round_match_expr = NULL_TREE;\n26055: \n26056: \t  if (match_expr == boolean_false_node)\n26057: \t    /* This sub-expression matches nothing: just wait for the next\n26058: \t       one.  */\n26059: \t    ;\n26060: \n26061: \t  else if (TREE_CODE (match_expr) == EQ_EXPR)\n26062: \t    {\n26063: \t      /* We are matching:  <discr_field> == <integer_cst>\n26064: \t\t This sub-expression matches a single value.  */\n26065: \t      tree integer_cst = TREE_OPERAND (match_expr, 1);\n26066: \n26067: \t      candidate_discr\n26068: \t       = analyze_discr_in_predicate (TREE_OPERAND (match_expr, 0),\n26069: \t\t\t\t\t     struct_type);\n26070: \n26071: \t      new_node = ggc_cleared_alloc<dw_discr_list_node> ();\n26072: \t      if (!get_discr_value (integer_cst,\n26073: \t\t\t\t    &new_node->dw_discr_lower_bound))\n26074: \t\tgoto abort;\n26075: \t      new_node->dw_discr_range = false;\n26076: \t    }\n26077: \n26078: \t  else if (TREE_CODE (match_expr) == TRUTH_ANDIF_EXPR)\n26079: \t    {\n26080: \t      /* We are matching:\n26081: \t\t   <discr_field> > <integer_cst>\n26082: \t\t   && <discr_field> < <integer_cst>.\n26083: \t\t This sub-expression matches the range of values between the\n26084: \t\t two matched integer constants.  Note that comparisons can be\n26085: \t\t inclusive or exclusive.  */\n26086: \t      tree candidate_discr_1, candidate_discr_2;\n26087: \t      tree lower_cst, upper_cst;\n26088: \t      bool lower_cst_included, upper_cst_included;\n26089: \t      tree lower_op = TREE_OPERAND (match_expr, 0);\n26090: \t      tree upper_op = TREE_OPERAND (match_expr, 1);\n26091: \n26092: \t      /* When the comparison is exclusive, the integer constant is not\n26093: \t\t the discriminant range bound we are looking for: we will have\n26094: \t\t to increment or decrement it.  */\n26095: \t      if (TREE_CODE (lower_op) == GE_EXPR)\n26096: \t\tlower_cst_included = true;\n26097: \t      else if (TREE_CODE (lower_op) == GT_EXPR)\n26098: \t\tlower_cst_included = false;\n26099: \t      else\n26100: \t\tgoto abort;\n26101: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333@baaf9b33ef307e3d2752a94e62274c374e6a5e20/-/blob/gcc/dwarf2out.cc%3FL25900-26100"}}}

\"path\": \"gcc/dwarf2out.cc\", \"symbol\": \"dwarf2out_finish\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"GCC generates DWARF debug information through a well-structured pipeline:\\n\\n## Debug Info Hook Interface\\nThe debug info hook interface is defined in gcc/debug.h as the `gcc_debug_hooks` structure. This structure contains function pointers that the compiler front-end calls during compilation. The key hooks include:\\n- `init()`: Initialize debug output\\n- `finish()`: Output final debug symbols\\n- `early_finish()`: Run cleanups after early debug generation\\n- `assembly_start()`: Called from cgraph_optimize before assembling functions/variables\\n- `early_global_decl()`: Called for global declarations during parsing\\n- `late_global_decl()`: Called after compilation for variables and functions\\n- `function_decl()`: Debug information for function declarations\\n- `type_decl()`: Debug information for type declarations\\n- `source_line()`: Record source file location\\n- `begin_prologue()`, `end_prologue()`: Prologue code markers\\n\\n## DWARF DIE (Debug Info Entry) Creation\\nThe DIE structures are defined in gcc/dwarf2out.h:\\n- `die_struct`: The main DIE structure (typedef'd as `dw_die_ref`)\\n- `dw_attr_node`: Represents DIE attributes (combination of attribute kind and value)\\n- `dw_val_node`: Represents attribute values with support for various types (addresses, offsets, location lists, constants, strings, references, etc.)\\n- `dw_loc_descr_node`: Represents location descriptions (sequences of stack machine operations)\\n\\nThe gcc/dwarf2out.cc file implements DIE creation functions:\\n- `new_die()`: Creates new DIE entries\\n- `gen_decl_die()`: Generates DIEs for declarations\\n- `gen_subprogram_die()`: Generates DIEs for subprograms/functions\\n- `gen_variable_die()`: Generates DIEs for variables\\n- `gen_type_die()`: Generates DIEs for types\\n- `gen_typedef_die()`: Generates DIEs for typedefs\\n- `gen_struct_or_union_type_die()`: Generates DIEs for struct/union types\\n\\n## DWARF Output Generation\\nThe main output generation file is gcc/dwarf2out.cc, which contains:\\n- `dwarf2out_init()`: Initializes DWARF debug output at the start of compilation\\n- `dwarf2out_early_finish()`: Finish early debug generation\\n- `dwarf2out_finish()`: Main function to emit complete DWARF information at end of compilation\\n- Functions to output DIE information and build abbreviation tables\\n\\n## Line Number Table Emission\\nLine number information is handled through:\\n- The `source_line()` hook in gcc_debug_hooks (called from final.cc during instruction scanning)\\n- Location tracking in dw_loc_list_struct and dw_loc_descr_node\\n- Variables and location lists maintain source file, line, and column information\\n- Final assembly output of line number information in DWARF sections\\n\\n## Assembly Output\\nThe gcc/dwarf2asm.cc and gcc/dwarf2asm.h files handle the low-level assembly output of DWARF information.\\n\\n## Call Frame Information (CFI)\\nThe gcc/dwarf2cfi.cc file implements DWARF call frame information, generating CFI instructions through the `dwarf2out_emit_cfi()` function.\\n\\n## Integration Point\\nIn gcc/toplev.cc, the compiler initializes `debug_hooks` to point to `dwarf2_debug_hooks` (the instance of gcc_debug_hooks structure initialized in dwarf2out.cc) debug info hook interface is defined in gcc/debug.h as the `gcc_debug_hooks` structure. This structure contains function pointers that the compiler front-end calls during compilation. The key hooks include:\\n- `init()`: Initialize debug output\\n- `finish()`: Output final debug symbols\\n- `early_finish()`: Run cleanups after early debug generation\\n- `assembly_start()`: Called from cgraph_optimize before assembling functions/variables\\n- `early_global_decl()`: Called for global declarations during parsing\\n- `late_global_decl()`: Called after compilation for variables and functions\\n- `function_decl()`: Debug information for function declarations\\n- `type_decl()`: Debug information for type declarations\\n- `source_line()`: Record source file location\\n- `begin_prologue()`, `end_prologue()`: Prologue code markers\\n\\n## DWARF DIE (Debug Info Entry) Creation\\nThe DIE structures are defined in gcc/dwarf2out.h:\\n- `die_struct`: The main DIE structure (typedef'd as `dw_die_ref`)\\n- `dw_attr_node`: Represents DIE attributes (combination of attribute kind and value)\\n- `dw_val_node`: Represents attribute values with support for various types (addresses, offsets, location lists, constants, strings, references, etc.)\\n- `dw_loc_descr_node`: Represents location descriptions (sequences of stack machine operations)\\n\\nThe gcc/dwarf2out.cc file implements DIE creation functions:\\n- `new_die()`: Creates new DIE entries\\n- `gen_decl_die()`: Generates DIEs for declarations\\n- `gen_subprogram_die()`: Generates DIEs for subprograms/functions\\n- `gen_variable_die()`: Generates DIEs for variables\\n- `gen_type_die()`: Generates DIEs for types\\n- `gen_typedef_die()`: Generates DIEs for typedefs\\n- `gen_struct_or_union_type_die()`: Generates DIEs for struct/union types\\n\\n## DWARF Output Generation\\nThe main output generation file is gcc/dwarf2out.cc, which contains:\\n- `dwarf2out_init()`: Initializes DWARF debug output at the start of compilation\\n- `dwarf2out_early_finish()`: Finish early debug generation\\n- `dwarf2out_finish()`: Main function to emit complete DWARF information at end of compilation\\n- Functions to output DIE information and build abbreviation tables\\n\\n## Line Number Table Emission\\nLine number information is handled through:\\n- The `source_line()` hook in gcc_debug_hooks (called from final.cc during instruction scanning)\\n- Location tracking in dw_loc_list_struct and dw_loc_descr_node\\n- Variables and location lists maintain source file, line, and column information\\n- Final assembly output of line number information in DWARF sections\\n\\n## Assembly Output\\nThe gcc/dwarf2asm.cc and gcc/dwarf2asm.h files handle the low-level assembly output of DWARF information.\\n\\n## Call Frame Information (CFI)\\nThe gcc/dwarf2cfi.cc file implements DWARF call frame information, generating CFI instructions through the `dwarf2out_emit_cfi()` function.\\n\\n## Integration Point\\nIn gcc/toplev.cc, the compiler initializes `debug_hooks` to point to `dwarf2_debug_hooks` (the instance of gcc_debug_hooks structure initialized in dwarf2out.cc)
